<Author>skylassie
<Content>Great valuefor your money! I am a flight attendant, so I have stayed in many hotels worldwide in my life, and I must say that I was pleasantly surprised wth the Carabela. Yes, I too read reviews before leaving and was skeptic, but I went with my mom, a very critical person, and she loved it. The food was exceptional, never got sick, and really enjoyed the A La Carte seafood restaurant. The room needed repairs, but who goes to the islands to stay locked up in their room? My 7yr old son, wasn't keen on the beach, but he loved playing ping pong every day and mini-golf too. There wasn't much for kids to do, but most children love pools, so that wasn't a big deal.We did a couple of the excursions. I do not recommend the one about swimming with the naturium for the elderly or the too young who have problems swimming. You must swim from the boat to the naturium and then back to the boat. So I spent $200 for 3 of us to stay on a boat for 5 hrs along with a few others who couldn't get off the boat due to medical issues. They were not impressed either. The inhabited island tour was beautiful. Went on a catamaran and spent the day on island and in natural pools in the middle of the ocean. Unbelievable! we could touch the bottom.Overall, I must say that out of all the hotels I have stayed in the Caribbean including some high end ones in Mexico, this one is great value for your money. To those people who expect to find the same amenities that they are accustomed to at home in a third world country, let go and enjoy yourself.My mom is planning her trip again, and she is definitely wanting to go back to the Carabela. Peace, quiet, great food, lovely beach, and great massages.

<Author>creatura
<Content>Great holidays! LOvely holidays - much better than expected while reading previous reviews!we were in Carabelle between 12th and 19th December 2008, and I have to say that it was a lovely holiday. I was very worried as first we bought this trip through the agency, and then I read reviews her eon trip adviser. I was really worried and constantly thinking how to cancel or to change the hotel. And probably this is why it was even bigger relief as everythign went smoothly and very nicely. It is a good 4 star hotel, in a very green environment, well maintened garden (and I was happy to see thta some other 5 star hotels were like in a sand desert), 3 swimming pools with open and workign bars (probably it depend son the season and tourist number?) - each pool has its own particularities and own advantages. Drink at the bar were mainly canned juices and soft drinks, but you can get fresh juice during the breakfast and it is normal that for food security reasons in such a heat it is not good to keep fresh juice. Lovely beach with palms, which is a great pleasure on a hot day, though of couse on a rainy or windy day it is better to stay in the pool. Lots of beacjh activities - palying volleyball, table tennis, football, sports, dancing, lots of animation during the day, and animation at 17h by the main swiming pool. It was a real family atmosphere, people enjoying company and very social, animators also great. Our kids (aged 4) enjoyed hight attention and smiles from all hotel staff - from bar men, gardeners, waitress in the restaurants. We had smile sand chats several times with each meal and whenever passing through, and so other kids. Mexican, Italian and international restaurants do exists!! (previous review writter said they don't.. probably he didn't find?;. you have to reserve in the mornign at the reseption and they'll show where it is located). Table's int he main restaurant were always nicely decorated with fruit figures and changes daily in harmony with evening show. Previous reader said no evening entertainmenty, but ther eis a show at 10 pm and then a disco. Meals were nice. At the very begining, we were not eating frutis and salads as we were afraid to get something, but after couple of days we couldn't resist any more and attacked fruits - no stomack problems for us or for kids! What I really loved, it was 10-16 kinds of breads!!! and when you cut your mornign bread loaf, you can still feel it is warm and home made - lovely touch! Black bread was particularly nice.The lovely thing is a good phootgrapher, passing everyday - with parrots or monkey, and we did some lovely photos. 8 USD per photo (big size), we also made soem personalised family pictures on the beach - and photographer was particularly professional with advices and combinations - we've done these lovely pictures as from the adds which will be framed and placed in the living room.Take on a possibility and go to Manati park - I do not like these tourist atractions, but one day was a bit cloudy and windy so instead of staying in the hotel room, we wen tto that park - kids and us enjoued all performaced and animals, swiming with dolphins and shows.. You can book it directly though the hotel and there is a bus 3 times per day directly from the hotel.The weakest point woudl be the rooms - nicely arrange sin old colonial style, wit strong local touch of colours (blue and red - not my tase, but that's the local spirit..) however rooms need some renovation, but it didn't bother us much as we were not staying in.Few moskitos in the evenings - so it wa sgood to have some creamI think a lot depends also on the season - if you are coming on the rainy season or not.. End December - March/April seam to be the bets time to travel -less windy, less rainy. Also, people suggest to go a bit to the North of the island in case it happens to be windy and rainy in punta cana.But most of all, the success of your holidays depends alot on our own approach to people, to environment - if we smile more, people do tend to smile to us too, and with a positive look averythign seems to be much better.I was scared to go to carabela, but indeed, we found lots of sports, animations, atractitions, great attention to kids, we madelost of freinds, participated in organized activities, had a nic emeal, nice beach, lovely memory photos done by professional photographer, nice animal park and etc. Great holidays, lots of smiles, nice memories - go and enjoy yourself!I was amazed to see people of all ages - young, single, travelling alone and with group of friends, families with kids and just single couples, mothers with prams as hotel is very suitable for prams or disabled - we also saw peope in vhielchairs, as well as middle aged couples, and elderly - this hotel has somethign to offer for everyone.

<Author>newbigginlad
<Content>Worst holiday ever For the past 2 years my wife and I were told by numerous people that the Dominican Republic was a great place to go for a quiet and relaxing holiday. So we decided to give it a go, and booked the Carabella Bavaro Resort.When we arrived at the Resort, we were greeted by a very polite person at the main desk who booked us in and organised a bellboy to take our luggage to the room. We thought then that this was going to be a lovely holiday. How wrong we were.On arriving to our room, the first thing we smelt when entering, was a musky damp odour. It was in the room the whole duration of the holiday, no matter how often we had the A/C on or windows open. The room was also very dated, the TV didnt have a remote. The room fridge only had a bottle of water in it, and all the resort information leaflets on the table were only written in Spanish.In the Bathroom, the towel rail was hanging off the wall, the bath had a red stain in it(at first we thought it was blood, but couldnt remove it). The bath and Toilet were also filthy, and the ceiling was falling through.There were 3 pools on the resort, all with a bar, the main pool had a swim up bar. The problem was, that the 2 other pools had bars but were never open, so not many people used these pools. And the main pool was always littered with dead insects and bits of thatch roof from the swim bar.The beach was nice, but always in the shade due to all the palm trees right up to the waters edge.The food was layed out beautifully, but didnt taste as well as it looked. And I fell victim to the dreaded stomach problems towards the end of the week. The so called Pizza parlour, Creperie and Mexican restaurants did not exist. The only place for food was the main restaraunt, or you could get a burger and chips on the beach.Apart from the man on the main entrance desk, the rest of the staff only spoke Spanish, and looked utterly miserable throughout our stay. It might have something to do with, the staff didnt seem to get a day off the the whole time we were there.There was no entertainment in the evenings, so if you wanted to do something after you had eaten in the evening. All you had was the bar. So it was back to the apartments to watch TV which we had never done before on a holiday anywhere.Im afraid the only thing enjoyable was the sunshine, which really was great.We wont be going back to the Dominican Republic again, all because this resort has put us off.

<Author>mad1663
<Content>Great for families This was the second time that I have traveled with my family to the Carabela Resort, and we were not disappointed. Having stayed at the resort before, we knew some of the reviews were correct that this would not be considered a 4.5 star resort by any means, but it is a resort that is well worth the money that you pay (and there are some FANTASTIC deals). The grounds are pretty and very clean, though the rooms are somewhat tired. We do recommend staying in the 10000 Block and request the third floor. The show from the auditorium can be heard very clearly from this area, but I can assure you that if you spend a full day swimming and participating in the many activities, there will not be much that can keep you awake.The beach is amazing and though the resort was very full, we always managed to find a spot on the beach close to the water to accomodate the six of us; my in-laws, my husband and I and our two teenage daughters. The Animacion crew (activities) are the friendliest and most congenial people we have ever met and got even us (La Familia) to participate in at least one activity every day.We have read reviews saying that people were unfriendly and that the housekeeping and service was poor, and we cannot disagree more. Tip your people. These people work long, long days with not much time off, and ANY gratuity is appreciated and you will be awarded gold status service. We tipped our waitress, and she would hold our 6 person table at the breakfast/dinner buffets by putting full cups on the table and she would remove them and wave us over when we arrived. We tipped our housekeeper and always came back to extra towels, towel designs and flowers/petals and an IMMACULATE room.Talk to the people who serve you and smile!! We never had a problem communicating with anyone.The food at the buffet was fantastic with many choices for both the picky eater and the more adventurous. We did not really care for the restaurant fare, so we stuck with the buffets for breakfast and dinner, and the beach snack bar for lunch. You will find the best french fries (rivaling the US) there, and my youngest fell in love with the fried fish. She didn't care WHAT kind of fish it was.For a day trip I cannot recommend the Tropical Storm highly enough. Carlos, the Captain, is engaging and entertaining, and his crew was a blast to party with. Sailing, singing, dancing, drinking, snorkeling, eating and sightseeing in the tropical sun; what more can you ask for......?Do not do the Glass Bottom Boat tour....enough said.Bottom line: we all had a great time and would go back in a minute.

<Author>Shirleyrajala
<Content>Not perfect, good value This is a place for beach lovers. We were there from April 13 to 20. We chose it because they said there were casinos in Punta Cana, but the one at Carabela didn't open until 9 at night, a little too late for us senior citizens. We found another one down the street that opened at 5, so we could go and play and still be back in time for dinner.I read all the reviews for the Carabela Resort, and felt a little uneasy about going there. But the price was the big deciding factor, and it was worth what we paid for it. Sure, the pillows were a little lumpy, the mattresses a little hard, but our room was immaculate and the grounds were spectacular. Everything worked in the room but we saw a few little ants around the sink one day, which was taken care of right away.The 3 pools were all very good, the drinks plentiful and easy to get, and although the food wasn't the best, the buffet was extensive; you could always find something to enjoy, the breads were wonderful, a huge array of fruits, and great ice cream.Communicating with the staff was sometimes a challenge because we only speak English, but never a real problem. The entertainment was repetitive but sometimes very good. Watching the beach activities we had a lot of respect for the crew, they provided a good time for those who played.We took an excursion off the resort to Saona Island, a wonderful experience, although not part of the all-inclusive. Again, beach lovers, the place to go.

<Author>MochaToronto
<Content>Very disappointing, but not all was lost We stayed at this hotel from March 21 - 28, 2008 and let me tell you, I wouldn't recommend this property. It wasn't terrible, but its definately not a 4 star.We arrived around 10:30pm Friday night, only to discover all restaurants and snack bars were closed. We were starved as we left Toronto at 4:30pm. Front desk told us to try the casino across the street (which is affliated with the hotel), and they would have snacks. The only thing they had were ham and cheese sandwichs, which we had to ask the bartender for. It took 20 minutes for him to give my boyfriend and I one sandwich each. When we asked for another sandwich, he refused. Terrible service.Reception at the hotel did not give extra room keys for each person in the room unless asked. They wouldn't let us rent a safe that night. We had to come back the next day.Rooms: the rooms were okay, but the beds were hard, sheets were very thin. Our beds were made each day, but despite tipping practically everyday, we only got a towel design once. The shower did not have complete coverage (only a half shower door) so each day our bathroom floor was wet. We didn't get extra towels and the towels were poor quality - we had towel fuss on out bodies everyday.Service: I found the service generally poor. Servers rarely smiled or greeted you. Only if generous tips were offered did we see any change in service, but there should have been a general standard of service which we didn't see. However, there was one exception, we had great service from Miguel, Carlos and Capitan at front desk. Miguel was generous enough to go with us into town on his day off.A la carte restaurants: There were 3 restaurants, mexican, italian and french. We enjoyed the mexican restaurant, but the resort failed to set the proper mood for each restaurant. The back ground music was often Reggaeton or Bachata - conflicting with the theme of the restaurant. Most cake desserts were awful. I found ordering fruits with ice cream the safest route. The wine tasted like vinegar. Bars: There were a variety of bars, but the skills and knowledge of creating cocktails by the bartenders was poor. We stuck to rum  coke, everything else tasted horrible. They did not use real fruit juices in cocktails like Rum punch or Sex on the Beach, which left a powdery after taste in your mouth.Entertainment: nightly entertainment was entertaining. However, there was no live music entertainment on stage or in any restaurant. I've travelled to many resorts and found this strange. The disco had a good DJ. Overall, the resort grounds were beautiful, but I'd give it 3 stars not 4.

<Author>Frederieke
<Content>quite pleasurable Having read the other reviews I wasn't expecting much from the food. And it was indeed not too good. Which is strange because the food was not cheap, it was just prepared strangely and usually too salty. However, I had great meals eating mostly fruit, which was fresh and abundant every day. There was fresh fruit juice of all kinds in the morning too. And friday's lobsternight was a nice surprise. There is a wide variety of food anyway, so you will not starve.I never tried any of the separate restaurants. I should have though, because they were a lot quiter. The buffet means that you enter in a room where about 150 people are eating and talking at the same time.Snacks were a disaster. I didn't like the soft-ice machine much either, it only had chocolate flavor and it tasted cheap. Same with drinks at the bars. The slush-machine distributed horribly acidy and sugary slush, but most people seemed to liked it. Most drinks are distributed in plastic cups, a big contribution to the local waste problem.The appartment was fine, big and with working airco. The television set was more of a problem but that didn't bother me. I had to change rooms once because I was at first located opposite a bar (La sirena) that had very loud music on all evening and night. Changing rooms was no problem. The room was kept clean very well. Sometimes it would have a bit of a sour or musty smell, but I couldn't determine if that was inside the room, or from outside. The beach was fine by me. It is true that there was a lot of shadow so you have to move your bed around. So if you are a large group it will be difficult to all catch the sun. There were enough beds on the beach. I didn't get hasseled by vendors, they are not allowed where the beds are. Beachtowels are provided by the hotel, but if you want to go to the beach after you've checked out, you will have to bring your own towel.I really disliked that when I walked around singly, I often got comments from the men working there. They would call me stuff like 'mi amor' or 'prinzessa'. I found it condescending. And what really annoyed me were the ridiculously short skirts of the girl-waiters at the buffet. When they bent over you could sometimes see their underwear. I found it degrading. Also, it made some of the older male tourist become too 'friendly' with the waitresses. I saw a waitress politely trying to ward off a too friendly hug from a senior tourist.I guess though that this kind of thing is connected with the country and the comparitive poverty of its people. But it is still very disagreeable to watch. Maybe you would have less of this in more expensive resorts.The resort was quite big and that was agreeable because you could have a walk around without running into people too much. Also there were parts of the beach that were relatively quite, no music from a bar or anything like that.I never cared for the animation so I don't know if it was good or bad. It did keep me awake untill eleven every night though.I never went to the pool because there were too many people there. Do not expect to find intelligent company here. But it is cheap and with the money you save you can get some delicious meals back home. The sun, the sea and the palmtrees are the same everywhere, so you might as wel go cheap and visit carabela beach resort.

<Author>MaineiacWestParis
<Content>Carabela Beach Resort  My husband, son (13) and I just returned from a week at the Dominican Republic where we stayed at the Carabela Beach Resort  Casino. We had a wonderful week and really enjoyed our stay. I would recommend this place to anyone, especially to families.We found the resort itself to be extremely clean, and the staff was very friendly and accommodating. The food was excellent at the buffet and we also enjoyed the individual resort restaurants on various eveings (Italian, Mexican and Gourmet). At the buffet you can make your own fajitas or have a chef make you a personalized omelet. There is an abundance of fruit and juices and unknown meats are marked by a picture of the animal on the platter (i.e. turkey, beef, rabbit, etc.) While this is self-serve, wait staff are there to remove your plates (keep your fork for second helpings or dessert) or bring you a drink. We really appreciated the buffet-style meals where you can eat as much as you like or just sit and sip a drink.Since there were three of us, the two queen beds (which were actually US double beds) were a bit cramped and we only had two energy saving bulbs in the two room lamps making the room quite dark. This was a frustration to me as I had brought books to read, but could only read on the deck, the beach or poolside during the day. (Tough life!) Other than that, our room was attractive, clean, and there was ample storage between the bureau and the large closet that housed a safe. ($10 for the week was worth it for peace of mind.) We often enjoyed the outside deck on our second floor room, and the television offered three channels in English for the one or two rainy afternoons or late evenings that we were lazing in the room. The cleaning staff was reliable. When they came late and it wasn't convenient for them to clean, we were left towels or extra toilet paper and a promise to be there earlier the next day. Face cloths are not provided, as I read on a previous post, so we took our own. If you have a portable drying rack, it might come in handy. We dried our bathing suits on the deck railing.The beach was wonderful! Yes, there are many trees that offer shade, but the swimming area has a smooth, sandy bottom and you can move your own chair anywhere to catch light or shade. For beach activities, we not only enjoyed the swimming, but took a snorkeling tour ($25 each for two hours) and our son went parasailing ($49 for the time of his life!) My husband had a long half-hour massage for $25.We also took a family safari trip which educated us about life as a Dominican and the production of coffee, chocolate and tobacco. My husband and son took a 4-wheeling tour of the places that the safari visited. Both excursions culminated in a swim at a beautiful beach where you can boogey-board.In the evening there is the opportunity to gamble at the casino and see a live musical show. We did both and watched at the casino as a friend won $300! While we were not so fortunate, we broke even and had an enjoyable evening, which culminated with the show.I had one slightly unnerving experience. The first time we went to our room with our luggage, my husband was putting the key into the doornob and the porter delivering our luggage just pushed the door open (as if helping us). Later, after we'd been to the beach and then to the pool nearest our room, I returned to the room and our key wouldn't work! I spoke to a nearby worker who took me to the room below ours which was where the key I had actually fit. We pushed open the door and I assured him it was not our room. First of all our things were not there, then the curtains were completely different and they were closed while we had left ours open; and someone else's sandals were just inside the door! I only speak a little Portuguese and he only spoke Spanish, of course, so between my Portuguese and English I was adamant that it was not our room, that ours was the one above and all of our things were there. (I had completely unpacked before we ventured to the beach.) He wanted to me to go into the darkened strange room with someone else's belongings and call the lobby. I told him that I would return with my husband, he handed me the key and we parted ways.The lobby said it was a mistake and gave us our true room key. Then I wondered about our door being pushed open by our porter in the first place, not to mention the fact that I had a copy of the key to the room below us. The next day I asked for a copy of our room key. I had to wait for a few minutes, but eventually got it. I wish to tell this story as a precaution. Despite how friendly the staff is, go with your instincts. On the plane trip home a woman told of a similar experience with discovering that their room key wouldn't fit and they arrived back at their place for the first time after midnight!We never had another issue and my husband thought I was too paranoid about this one. It all worked out and we really enjoyed our week at the Carabela Beach Resort.Oh yes! I think using a credit or debit card is wise. Or at least don't be so quick to spend your dollars, but go to an ATM and be educated about the exchange rate. I just looked at my on-line bank records. People were paying $8 in cash for a slice of pizza at the airport just yesterday. I used my debit card and it was $4.50. Also, when I used the Internet at the hotel, I paid 150 pesos, about $4 and when our son paid cash, he paid $6!Hope this review helps people to have fun while also being smart!

<Author>loveTtravel
<Content>will be back to Punta Cana, but will not go back to this resort. My husband, and I just got back from Carabela resort yesterday 4/6/07. We went with our girls ages 8 and 10. We love going to the Caribbean, have been going every year for 15 years, and we are not picky people. I will start with the check in and go through our whole experience.Front Desk: not very friendly and speak very little English.Rooms: we were in the 5100 building, on the second floor. We had a beautiful ocean view. The rooms are very plain, there was 2 full sized beds, very uncomfortable beds, lumpy old pillows that smelled moldy. A 19 inch TV, with one or two English channels, the rest Spanish, French and German. Balcony door and screen very hard to open and close, kept getting stuck, the screen door had many ripped areas, but they changed it 24 hours after we called them. No iron or board, or coffe maker in room. there is a safe, for $10 per wk, I highly recommend you get it, a gold ring was taken from my make up bag (I forgot to put it in the safe). The bath room tub was old and chipped in many places, No wash cloth provided, so take your own. The rooms were cleaned every day and they did a good job, but did not speak English at all. Food: was just O.K. Left over lunch was usually recycled at dinner. for example steamed vegetables from lunch would become breaded deep fried vegetables, grilled lamb would be lamb stew at night, etc. The coffee is dispensed from machines, which mixed coffee flavored liquid with hot milk (No fresh brewed coffee). No coffee served at lunch. The reservation only restaurants were usually fully booked by 9 AM. You had to get there at 7 AM to get a reservation. Their food was not any better than the Buffet. We got sick after eating at the Italian restaurant. Pools: they have 3 pools, Not too clean, and if you don't get there early in AM, you'll have a hard time finding a pool chair. They give you one card per person at check in for beach towels, which you pick up at the beach. If you loose a towel or the card, you are charged for the towel. The towels are well guarded by the Towel Nazi, and you are only allowed one clean towel per day. Bars/drinks: Not good at all. Mixed drinks all tasted the same. The bartenders were nice, but don't speak English.Beach: The only wonderful part of this hotel was the beach. Beautiful white sand and lovely water. Plenty of beach chairs available.Check out: No problem with check out. went smoothly. I hope this is helpful.  
<Date>Apr 8, 2007

<Author>DanDon85
<Content>Foreign Intruders! My best friend and I decided to take our first vacation without our parents. We chose to go to the dominican republic and stay at this resort. I was only 20 and she was 22. Filled with excitement we arrived at the resort and checked it ... A thrid floor room on the corner of the building with a balcony and a gorgeous view. Our first night there at about 3am we heard pounding on our door but we didn't have a peep hole to look out of to see who it was. We hadn't met any new friends yet, so we didn't answer the door. Shortly after that we heard noises coming from our balcony. Us being half asleep we didn't pay much attention to it. We assumed it was a bird or a peacock that we had seen many of on the resort. We then heard our LOCKED sliding door pop open and the curtian swoosh around. Another traveler staying at the resort who was highly intoxicated ran into our room and started yelling. Neither of us knew what to do. He left our room seconds after and I then called the security. NONE of which spoke a word of english. The security we saw standing on the beach w/ machine guns straped around their shoulders apparently didn't see this man climb up 3 balconies and finagle his way into our room. The security could not understand what we were saying..at 3am they called the owner of the resort to come immediately because my friend and I were hysterically crying and didn't know what to do. He arrived and was very nice to us. Demanded that a security guard stand on our balcony, at our front door, and down below by the pool where the man began climbing until the morning when he could change our location on the resort. I wanted to take the next flight home to Boston, but we decided to change our room to a different building. As the owner was showing us various rooms, we saw the man who came in our room. They questioned him and he admitted to doing it. Him and his 4 friends were kicked off the resort and banned from coming back. It re-assured me a little bit but for the rest of my vacation I was paranoid. Not a way to spend relaxing time. Security there apparently does not do their job. The put up a good scare with their guns hanging from their shoulders but don't act upon people climbing up balconies. The resort was beautiful and the entertainment was great, but I wont go back to the Dominican Republic again... My dad said it wasn't a good idea, maybe next time I should actually listen - God only knows what could have happend to us! I thank my lucky stars =)

<Content>Won't Be Going There Again I am by no means a 5 star traveller so this review is going to sound like I am hoity toity but thats not the case at all.We have been to the Dominican 3 times and have not encountered a hotel like this. Most of our trips have been very last minute so we are usually in a 3 maybe 3.5 star so we felt very fortunate to be going to whats rated a 4 star hotel.Well if this hotel is a 4 star then the 3 stars that we previously stayed at must have been a 6 star.First impression was the rude front desk staff. They spoke not a word of English so was very difficult to try and explain that we requested our 3 rooms on the same floor. After trying to communicate this we ended up on different floors and Thank God we were on the main because the elevators don't work and I requested a building with an elevator due to having very bad knees.Our rooms were very average and there were no matteress pads on the beds. Just a very thin sheet over the matteress which was really gross. Our tv was a very old 12 inch where the room next to us had a big 27 inch. Not that we are there to watch tv but I like to put my camera in the jacks to review the pictures that were taken. The washroom had ants on the counter and no matter how hard you tried to kill them there were always more.We tipped our maid with gifts and dollars and they took them without a problem but nothing was done in the room that would show apperication,the basic clean up and she was out of there. I had seen her in the hall way as she cleaned the room across the hall and I tried to explain that I wanted a clean glass she spoke no english either, So when I finally got through to her what I wanted she went to the room she was cleaning and took a glass off the dresser went to the washroom and rinsed it then brought it out to her cart and dried it with a dirty towel then handed it to me. Talk about grossed out.The food in the buffet was always pretty much the same not alot of variety. They would change it daily but then make supper with what was left over from lunch. 5 out of the 6 of us got ill and that sure put a damper on the trip.The beach itself well thats another story. It was very shaded with natural palm trees which were nice if you were there for shade.TO get sun you had to go to the lower part of the beach that was not very wide you you ended up getting wet cause the waves usually made it to the top of the lower beach. For the shaded area of the beach there were tree needles from a certain tree that was there and it had little pine cone things that were very sharp they were everywhere which made walking the shaded areas hard on the feet if you were barefoot. Also the smokers of the resort thought they had their own personal ashtray cause the beach was littered in butts. Nasty... Really Nasty,I spoke to our rep about upgrading to another hotel which was a total waste of time. He looked at me like I had 3 heads and asked why I would want to leave. I gave him all the reasons and he said there was nothing he could do. That every hotel was booked solid. I didn;t believe him and I questioned him on it and he got quite snotty with me. As it turned out we ended up staying at the hotel, He said it was a 4 star but we just happened not to pay the preimum price, and had we then we would be in a much nicer room. Well its funny that the hotel is a 4 star shouldn't it be a 4 star all the way through??.The language barrier was the hardest to deal with the hotel really catered to the Europeans and left the English people to fend for themselves.So thats my take on the hotel if you have any questions please feel free to email me and I will be more then happy to give you an honest opinion.Thanks Linda majestic_4u@yahoo.com

<Author>woodski
<Content>Enjoyed It visited the carabela bavaro beach resort in punta cana for 10 days in late april to early may. what a great experience. room was clean, had a great 2nd story view of the beach and ocean. food was wonderful , except for the beach snack bar, which only served pizza and goat burgers. maybe hot dogs. specialty restaurants were wonderful. never had a problem getting a reservation. had problems with the air conditioner, but someone always came promptly to fix it. come to find out, it wasn't broken at all. every time we opened the sliding doors, the unit would shut down. air only runs when door is shut. boy did we feel stupid. loved the beach and the ability to always get chairs, towels or an umbrella. played all the games on the beach, danced and won 5 bottles of rum. the theater was very good, with a lot of audience participation. gym didn't have a tread mill. but we walked the extensive grounds, along with the peacocks. met wonderful people. a couple from new hampshire are meeting us this april in the mayan riviara, for 10 days. we would definitely go back to this resort, but for now want to visit different places. drinks too strong, so may want to ask them to let up on the liquor. great clean pools. only one thing we did't like. many of us got bug bites (i didn't) on our legs. don't know what it was maybe mosquitos or sand fleas? when you do go, enjoy and take advantage of all the resort has to offer. connie and dick from vermont

<Author>angeljill7
<Content>A very nice getaway DON'T PAY ATTENTION TO ALL THE BAD REVIEWS FOR THIS HOTEL! My boyfriend and I (age 24  23) just got home from the Carabela Beach Resort  Casino and had an amazing time. We were a little nervous going down because of the reviews we had read, but when we got there we loved it! People complain about the food but you have to realize, you are in a developing country, not the Ritz Carlton. You obviously don't eat all the different meats they serve at meals unless you would like to get sick. The buffet had plenty of options so if the dinner they were serving wasn't the best, you could always go to the pasta bar, the salad bar, etc.. We thought the facilities were evry nice. Everything was very clean. Some of the reveiews we read said the bathrooms weren't clean, but they were completly wrong. the only problem I saw is some of the stalls were out of toilet paper, but that happens. We stayed in the most centrally located building, rm 2210. From our balacony we had a nice view of vegetation and the main pool  pool bar. From our room would could just go downstairs and be right at the buffet, lobby  main pool. It was about a football field walk to the beach, if that. The beach had plenty of natural shade because of beautiful palm trees. There was a storm one night off shore so the water was a little rough the next day, but besides that the weather was perfect.The other great feature of this place was everywhere you turned, you could find a bar easily. The local rum is very good and there is a blender at every bar. Also conveniently located at these bars was self serve spring water, soda and juice. When you are at the beach there are is one hut with self serve beer, juice, smoothies, soda  water, a regular bar with a bartender and the snack bar. The snack bar doesn't have tons of options, but it gets the job done. In there you can get self serve beer, juice, soda water, hamburger, htodogs, french fries, pizza and soft serve ice cream. We didn't try the hamburgers or hotdogs, but the french fries, pizza and ice cream was great when you needed a little snack in between meals.We went out on the snorkeling excursion from the hotel for only $29 and they took us to a beautiful coral reef. It was definitly worth the money.A couple nights we went to the casino, which is technically across the street, les than a 1 minute walk form the main lobby, but the whole area is lit. The fornt of the casino has fancy lights and water. The casino was a little small, but fun. We got there right when it opened at 9 and hit the roulet tabel. There were a bunch fo different tables as well as slot machines and a bar.The websites says everyone speak English, which is pretty much true when it comes to the hotel staff, btu a majority of the guests are European. Most can speak English, some chose not to. I think we may have been the only American couple there at the time. We did find some Canadians, who we befriended, buit besides that, don't expect everyone to be speaking English.All in all, we had a great time. Participate in activities on the beach and the show at night because if you win something, they love to give away bottles of rum! I would definitly recommend this place. I feel as if the price we paid for this vacation ($699/person all-inclusive) was a very very good deal for what we got. The onyl thing I would say to travelers going is don't expect to be at a 5 star American hotel, because there is a difference. But if I could go abck there right now, I would in a second.

<Content>All good except the coffee We stayed at the resort in March 2006. There were only a few english speaking people there. We are from Canada. I was appaled that others from other countries did not even try to communicate with us. The only bad thing was the coffee. Please don't call that machine that turns out some kind of hot water with coffee flavour, coffee. I know that coffee beans are grown here and a great cup of coffee could be made if they would take the time to brew it. We stayed in block 10 and had a great time. We went on 3 tours and recommend them to every one. I think that it needs to be brought to the hotel management that they need a grill to make the hotdogs and hamburgers so some of them have flavour. All in All this is a nice resort, older but has charm and very central. Enjoy

<Author>Ctlin
<Content>Great for first time I decided now to write this review because I really saw how helpfull they are...We've been to Carabela from 11/06/2004- 11/14/2004 on an all inclusive plan. The resort was rated 4.5 starz and I think it almost deserve that. They were extending their construction(probably they are done by now). We found a lot of helpfull tips on [----]You have to tip the guy at the front office(reception)-$10 to give you the 'best room ocean view' - we did and we were happy with the roomThe food is ok, you should go to the a la carte restaurants-0 especially El Almirante -very good food and serviceBring a lot of $1 bills - for cleaning lady, for the bar (always tip the same guy - I use to give $1 when I arrived and $1 when I left-usually with something to go...)It's a very nice and quiet place, good for fammilies- they don't have a kids club-just a playground- but sometimes we would let our kids there with one of the security guys- there is a lot of them - that's why the beach is ok, nobody from outside can come on resort grounds--that was the bestWe went shopping around for souvenirs- you have to bargain a lot. We bought a big caracol (the big shell) and some paintings and statues(small) for less than 1/4 of what they asked. Don't show them big bills- go shopping with $1 and $5 billslearn some spanish- they are friendly when you talk to them --almost nobody understands englishHave fun nomater what!

<Author>Beverley
<Content>Always enjoy Punta Cana We recently spent 1 week at the Carabela Bavaro Beach resort at Punta Cana. October 21st ?28th.My husband and I decided to opt for the most reasonable hotel on offer, through the Spanish Company, Pullmantur. Our past 3 visits had been with the tour operator, Travelplan. (1st visit Bavaro Princess, 2nd visit Sunscape Punta Cana Grand and 3rd visit Punta Cana Princess All Suites). Our 4 hour check-in at Madrid airport was a bit of a pain, but as we had to fly in from Mlaga, we were happy to check in the luggage as soon as possible.We travelled on a Boeing 747, and the travel time was 8 hours.We felt very smug at Punta Cana airport, with our zip-off trousers ?we would recommend these to everyone who is travelling from cooler climes. They seem to have improved the passport control here, they now just need to get the ladies in their fancy outfits to move people along a little quicker from their photo opportunity as this meant there was quite a queue just to get into the airport arrivals building.We were directed to our bus over on the other side of the car park, waited about half an hour for the stragglers to arrive, then we were off. The whole coach was going to our hotel, so there were no stops at various hotels to do numerous drop-offs, which was a blessing.Check in at the hotel was no probem, and there was a note on their form that we had requested a top-storey, sea-facing room, as I had heard nothing from my emails I actually called, so I would recommending doing both, just to be on the safe-side. We did not wait for a porter as there were bags appearing from every which way, so we just saw ourselves to our room, which was in block 5, 4th floor (with lift), no. 9.The air-con was thankfully running, with an additional room key when we arrived. It looked clean, if a little basic. There was loud meringue music playing from a bar in El Cortecito, which is directly next door. Saying that the music never bothered us, it just reminded us where we were, which is a country we adore. The view from our room was straight out to sea, but, and this will sound silly, we had most of the view obscured, because of all the coconut trees?tops being right on the same level as we were, so it might be better to ask for a 3rd floor room. Also I agree with other reviews that Block 6 would be the ideal Block to stay in. The bathroom was very basic, and we were missing plugs both in the bath tub and the sink. The other complaint we had were the pillows, which looked quite old and dirty. The new pillows arrived straight away via housekeeping (although they were still of the lumpy variety) and the plugs arrived the next day. We dashed down to the beach to have a swim on the day of our arrival and the sea was as beautiful as ever, warm and blue, so we were quite happy with our choice.Restaurants:Buffet: Open-air. Good at breakfast, lunch and dinner - always had plenty of choice, self-service drinks, couple of theme nights (eg. Spanish  Dominican while we were there) ?one night they even had a sushi chef. Beware the unlevel floor surface, I nearly fell several times. Restaurant bookings are made at breakfast time near the main entrance of the buffet. Never a problem getting a booking and there is no limit on bookings, although you are restricted to only booking one day at a time.Gourmet: Next to the buffet restaurant. Air-conditioned, which was welcome. Very nice menu ?shame you cannot order cocktails as a drink in the a la carte options.Mexican: Lovely on the beachItalian: Very nice ?had one of our nicest meals hereCreperie: In the Italian ?avoid this ?as only had savoury crepes on the menu, nothing else. So we ended up having the buffet after on the night we ate there.Day-time snack bar on the beach ?RUBBISH - ok for self service drinks, but the burgers were hideous, more like corned beef, without the beef. 4 things on the menu (even with a photo of each item, looking really sad)?1.chips / 2. Burger /3. Hot Dog / 4. Pizza ?One day we did have a hot dog roll with some chips on and it was actually delicious. This was one of the things we put in the suggestion box at the hotel. Even a selection of fruit would have been great.Our day was basically, breakfast, back to room to brush teeth, down to beach to set up camp for the day, scuba diving every other day, quiet pool near block 6 for sundowners (coffee in our case, as we are not big drinkers, the bar was not open here, but we would get drinks from the close-by block 10 bar) and swim in Block 6 pool as it was so peaceful and the water was far warmer than any of the other pools. Back to room for rest then bath prior to evening. Remember your bug spray!!! Restaurant then show. The disco looked OK, and we were surprised that they had water free for all, as were under the impression it was pay-pay all the way in there.Other points we were both aware of:Good: Excellent mini-golf round by the gym next to the kids club ?clubs and balls from inside the gym, or sometimes the kids club.Nice Self-serve coffee, soda, juice and pina colada  coco loco at most of the barsLaid-back atmosphere They supplied a 1 gallon bottle of water for your room fridge, although we are used to having soft drinks supplied in the mini fridge.Poor:Shows were worse than most we had seenIf you got peckish for food, there was nothing around the opening hours of the restaurants.If you were a night bird, finishing at 12 clock would not be ideal.No bottled water, only horrible water fountains all over the resort, which reminded me of work!Beach was not set out at all and you were left to drag your beds off a pile in the morning. As we walked along and passed the Palladium next door the layout on the beach was much better. Swim up bar was only operating on the reverse side, so you had to get a drink and drop into the pool with it. We did not spend any time at this bar.To sum up, we really could not complain for the price we paid, and found everyone very pleasant around the resort. We will definitely be returning to Punta Cana and to be honest if we found a deal like this again, we would probably opt for this resort again, as prefer to spend the difference on diving.

<Author>LastMinuteGirl
<Content>A Good Deal for the Money I enjoyed a one week holiday at Carabela last December with my family who gathered at the resort for a reunion, and this was my 5th trip to the DR, (I have also been to Jamaica, Cuba, Mexico and the Cayman Islands). Although there were only 8 of us, the hotel accommodated us in the same building and arranged for my parents to be on the ground floor due to medical/health reasons. The staff was very pleasant and we found the food to be just fine at the buffet and quite decent at the a la carte restaurants. The rooms were always clean and everything seemed to work well (light/water etc.), just don't bring food to the room as you may encouter a trail of ants. The beach was great as we could choose between the shady areas or full sun area and the water was beautiful. It has a quaint little town adjacent if one likes to shop for souveniers, get snacks at the local grocery store, or even get a hair cut at the local barber as my boyfriend did for very little cost (they did a good job too). It is a fairly low key resort, great for relaxing, (I didn't check out the nightly entertainment), so if you're looking for lots of action, keep looking. I would go back to Carabela again since it's not overly expensive as it usually rates as a 3 star.  
<Date>Sep 29, 2006

<Author>yetsenia777
<Content>Loved it and can't wait to go back! My boyfriend and I went to the Carabela Resort and it was quite the experience! My boyfriend is white and am puerto-rican and he was very nervous and it worked out perfectly. There are people down there that are very fleunt in several languages; spanish of course, english, french, and german. When you arrive you have to get everything checked like any airport and pay $10.00 each in US dollars for your tourist fee, don't put it away they are going to ask for it before you leave the airport.(They actually ask for it and shred it)Why? Who knows? Then after that you are about to leave and all you see is a swarm of people trying to get you to go with them. Please make sure you hold on to your bags and if you are going to let someone help you do not lose sight of it. After that its the craziest ride of your life! I don't know what the speed limit is but they drive fast and crazy. When we go to the Resort they where very fast and efficient and we had a great room! Buiding 10 a new building and it was great! The balcony view was perfect. They have a buffet which was great different varieties which I loved! Now these are the times for the buffet breakfast 7am-10am, lunch 12pm-3pm, dinner 7pm-10pm. There is also a snack bar we never went but i didn' t hear any complaints. They also have three restuarants that you do have to make reservations for call a day in advance they fill up quick. Now quick basic things that you might want to know; get a safe its definitely worth it, calls are pricey $1.00 connect fee, t.v. does have basic channels so you won't feel to distant from home. One quick thing this resort has a beautiful beach and a great view and atmospere. Before I forget theres Atms there but they give you pesos only so don't even use it. Theres a bank at the front desk they can change money for you. One US dollar is (37.60) in pesos. Doesn't do much trust me. You can also buy souvenirs at the resort not to much of a price difference from buying outside. The weather is very humid very hot. There are the occasional thunderstorms that last about 10 mins. max. The pools are great and clean and let me not forget very warm. We had a great tourist representive if you wanna do any outside activities you should always go through them. They are alot safer. We would definitely recommend an excursion we went to Soana Island that was amazing and affordable. Water is clear and sand is white. My overall experience for both of us was amazing I would reccomend this resort anytime to any one. So I hope you like it and travel safe always. Adios!

<Author>NS_Highlander
<Content>The food made us sick The only thing that would ever stop me from going back to the resort is the food borne illness that permeates this resort and the whole country. I had no problem with the variety or the taste or presentation of the food, but if I am getting sick than we have a very big problem.   First of all for any Nay Sayers, it was NOT the alcohol. I did not drink much of it as I was doing all I could do to stay hydrated to counter the effects of illness.  This was not a stomach bug or virus and neither am I prone to this sort of thing as I ate Cafeteria food for 4 years in university and have lived on military food for months at a time. I never got these types of problems when others did. I have traveled for weeks at a time in the British Isles drinking my face off every night and have never had anything that even resembles this.  I am also not the only one. My wife was affected, as well as everyone at the resort who came over on the same plane. One such individual has very extensive experience in the food service industry. I really hope he will post a review as he noticed many problems with how food is handled.  I met a German guy who stayed in his room for 4 days after he got sick. My wife saw a little down syndrome girl vomiting at the pool. When at the variety show I looked around to see 90% of people drinking water, and not alcohol. Could this be a sign of food borne illness induced dehydration? I wonder what the problem is. Is that the food they buy is bad? Do they not cook it enough? Do they cross contaminate? Is there inadequate refrigeration? Is it poor hygiene and hand washing? Are they cooking with infected tap water? Are they reusing food from a previous meal? Does the hot stay hot and the cold stay cold? Is it all of them at the same time? I realize this is a budget resort. The food isn the best quality in the world and the liquor is of the worst quality and full of sugar. However, this comes with the territory of booking a 3 star resort. However, food poisoning is not something that any person should have to endure. Most of the problems seem to be related to meat. I would not feed a pet dog much of what is being served at that resort. Who wants to go to a resort and just eat rice and bread? Every time that you sink your fork into the food there, it feels like your stomach is playing Russian roulette. I would like the Carabela resort to post a rebuttal and explain what they are going to do to alleviate this problem.  Other than the food, I was happy with the resort in general. My only other complaint was that some of the public bathrooms at the resort were always filthy and should be better maintained. The bed was hard, but supportive. The beach was fine. The staff was great, and the smaller sized resort had an intimate feel. There was enough to do that we were seldom bored. I would this a good resort for young people and families. If I were retirement age I probably would not want to stay here. At the end of the day, if you like paying for alcohol you are too sick to drink and relish going to the bathroom a dozen times a day (with toilet paper reminiscent of 300 grit sandpaper) or eating Imodium AD and having pains in your stomach because your body is now being forced to harbor this toxic food, than the Dominican Republic and this resort is for you!  I am passing on this complaint to the Dominican department of tourism and if anyone feels that food borne illness is something that is going to prevent you from coming to the Dominican Republic, in all fairness you should let them know so they can do something about it. The country has special tourist police, but apparently not special tourist health inspectors. In the age of Mad Cow and Avian flu, food borne health issues are a much bigger threat to tourists than street crime. Write the tourist board at this address. http://www.dominicanrepublic.com/Tourism/english/contact_us.kp.html  FOODBORNE ILLNESS IS UNACCEPTABLE IN ANY COUNTRY, AT ANY RESORT. UNLESS PEOPLE FIGHT BACK, RESORTS WILL NEVER CHANGE AND CONTINUE TO COMMIT THE SAME PRACTICES THEY HAVE DONE FOR YEARS. IT IS TIME TO HIT THEM WHERE IT HURTS?THE POCKET BOOKsbohandley@yahoo.ca

<Content>Resort Was GREAT!!! We had a WONDERFUL time. The resort was fine. Yes one of the smaller ones, but we did visit some of the bigger resorts and you need a bus to go from one end to the other they are so big. We enjoyed the cozy intimate feel. We did not spend a lot of time at our hotel room or the resort so the little nit picky items mention did not bother us. We were in the Caribbean and we planned to make the best of it and that is just what we did.Service was excellent. You are in a Spanish speaking country why do you expect and assume they will be fluent in English? It's all inclusive how much Spanish do you really need to know anyhow? Order you drinks and if you get use to a certain drink type the bartender will just keep 'em coming and buffet you serve yourself and the restaurants have English on the menus.BTW servasa is beer in Spanish. And at many of the food stands the beer is self service on tap. The pools were terrific. We stayed at the main pool with the swim up bar.We booked through TNT travel and did several of the adventure tours; jeep safari tour to the sugar can fields, villages, cigar factory, visit to the island of Soana located on the Caribbean Sea, the water is turquoise clear blue and so beautiful and that sand is pure white, we also went to the capital Santo Domingo and visited the caves, when to a Dominican restaurant and had the best food ever. In addition we went horse back riding. We planned to have a blast and our expectations were exceeded. We will definitely go back.If you plan to go and just stay at the resort the entire time then I recommend a higher end resort with many more options. But where ever you end up staying remember its up to you to make the best of it.Bon Voyage!!!

<Content>Awful service, arrogant staff I just came back from a one week stay at Carabela. What a regretful experience ! Even though it is supposed to be a 4 star hotel, in my book, it only rates a 2 star hotel, and believe me, I am not a difficult customer. From my arrival until my departure, the bad experiences were unfortunately accumulating. Upon arrival, my room was filled with water due to an air conditioning problem. I had to insist to change rooms and get a functional one, because they refused to do so. The service of the staff was very rude and arrogant. For exemple, when you have to make a phone call, you have to dial 0 for the reception and they will connect you. So many times, the receptionist would answer that he has no time right now and to call back in 5-10 minutes. He also would hang up when he realised that it was about a phone call that the client had to make. I went a couple of times to the front desk to ask why he would hang up on me and he would just simle saying that he doesn't have the time to make connections for the clients. When I asked his name, he gave me a false name so I was never able to make a proper complaint. By the way, they do not wear name tags so they can not be identified ! Everybody covered for eachother, so there was no way to get your point across to anyone.At the restaurant, the food was OK, however, no service. Nobody comes to fill up your water or ask you if you want anything to drink. I had brought sufficiant 1$ bills to give in tips, and for the first time ever, I didn't have to leave any tips at the table since during the entire week, nobody came to serve us. We had to go to the bar and get our own drinks.The beach is not as nice as other hotels. I guess do to previous storms it became multileveled (not straight). You have to jump down form one level to another to get to the water.I travelled many times to the south and I have to qualify this as the worst experience ever ! I would not recommend this hotel to anyone !

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Memorable vacation I just came back from Carabela with a friend and barely have any complaints. It took us 2 days to get to know the place and the staff. The food was good for the first 2 days, then it got so so, but it is a poor country and they really do try their best to satisfy the guests. The Mexican restaurant a la carte was great (you get 3 reservations per week but if you get friendly with the staff they will sneak you in with a smile!!! Thank's Julio)The entertainment at night was not amazing but some dancers are really good and they did try to make us laugh and some of their shows were really funny. They organized many activities during the day (on the beach and at the pool area) they always tried to get us to have fun dancing to El Mariachi. THE BAR: if you really want to have a good time there, make friends with Nicholas, Pablo and Julia they are a great bunch. Nicholas will entertain you to the point that you will be sad when they close the bar at midnight, but ask them to meet you at the disco and they will make you dance all night. The rooms were ok, we didn't spend much time there so we really didn't care about it much. the air conditioning was working great (freezing at night!) the room was always clean. If you leave a tip the mades will do extras 9nice designes on the beds, extra towels, they even picked up our clothes and folded them on the chair for an extra chocolate candy :) In overall i really enjoyed myself there. it is not the best hotel i've been to but i had a lot of fun there (especially thanks to the great staff) i read a review that mewntiond that they were racist, well i've seen some tourists treating them like dogs, so i'm not surprised thet they can be bitter sometimes. We didn't have any problems there, give a smile, be polite, try to talk to them instead of just demending whatever you need and they will truly make your vacation memorable, like mine.

<Author>chicahalifax
<Content>Very Satisfied We found the Carabela to be very satisfying for the price we paid for it. It is not a luxury resort and valet service but it is not a low-graded resort either. Rooms and buildings were adequate. Grounds were impeccable and staff was always at work on them. The size of the hotel was appealing as it never seemed crowded anywhere like other 800-1000 room resorts. I was told the hotel was full when I was there and I never had a wait for anything, buffet at meal times, etc.Dining room service at buffet was a-1 with plates cleared from tables immediately. We did not do the a-la-cartes as we dont like to committ to meal times. Food was plentiful, with lots of variety, and replenished when needed. The self-service drink area at the buffet is a good idea and cuts down on staff having to wait on people at their table. Help yourselves folks.....we are not totally lame when we are on vacation.The only down-fall was with the beach but we adapted to it and made out fine. Beach area is majority treed which some may like - there is a small totally sun area in front of the treed area by the waterside. This is where we located ourselves and found it to be ample space. Beach chairs were ample and we never had to reserve them early in a.m, however we were at beach most mornings by 8 a.m.Having the town el corticito next to the resort was nice for a change of pace - to go over and look/walk around.Security was visibly present however no problems were noted during the entire 2 weeks we were there.The front of the hotel is right on a main street with local bus service stopping right in front of the resort which is very convenient. Bus fare is much less than taxi fare and very safe.....the local people even tell you where to get off if you ask them.Overall, all staff I dealt with were friendly and helpful.....For the price paid I was very satisfied and would definitely return to this resort. I love the central location and am not inclined to being fussed upon or pampered at all times. I do speak limited spanish and find this makes a huge difference. After all we are in their country, why should we expect them to speak our language. If a tourist comes to your country are you expected to speak their language?

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A LOVELY RESORT - Don't be scared away!!!!!! Okay... I'm American, and my boyfriend is Canadian, so you're getting two different cultural opinions in this review..... I don't usually read (or write) reviews, but I feel compelled this time to put my two-cents in. I've traveled extensively throughout the Caribbean, but have never bothered to read reviews as I believe that any place (or experience) is entirely skewed by one's own personal interpretation (hey, we're all different, right???). So the reason I did read the reviews here was because I have to admit I was concerned by what (seems to me) to be such an extremely low price for an all-inclusive resort. So, after reading all the negative reviews, it was with some trepidation that my boyfriend and I first stepped foot onto the Hotel Carabella grounds. WELL -- we worried needlessly. The hotel was beautiful and we had a GREAT time. Again, every experience, food (geez, even a sunset), will be viewed and judged differently according to a person's own tastes and preferences. So I'm not saying anyone is wrong here, BUT COME ON!!!!! I would definitely recommend this hotel, and I think some of the reviews here were unnecessarily harsh. The beach was beautiful; the grounds were wonderful and so well-kept; the help were friendly, gracious, and helpful (of course you'll always run into one or two not so friendly people -- ANYWHERE YOU GO!); the food was fine (and we ate pretty much everything they offered with no ill-effects from the food!); the little village next to the resort was fun to go through; the drinks were plentiful (tip from my Canuck boyfriend which I loved: bring a large plastic beer mug from home so you don't have to keep going back for another tiny disposable cup of beer - the bartenders are very happy to oblige you by filling your mug to the brim); the pools were clean and pretty; what the heck more do you want?? Okay, so the room left a bit to be desired, it's entirely true and I agree with others on this point... but we weren't there to spend time in our room. I would gladly trade having a posh room that I don't spend time in but to sleep, for the loveliness of the resort (and certainly for the very low PRICE!) We were lucky, though, as our air conditioning did work perfectly (it actually got TOO cold for me). Yes, the shows were boring and the two times we went, it was just the same dancing put to different music. But what else do they do when they're catering to so many different languages? You can't have a comedy show, or a variety show, when you'll have to repeat everything in 10 different languages! Think about it! My boyfriend and I enjoyed the experience of being a minority when it came to speaking English. It was a neat experience for us. But again, we were there to spend time with each other and it didn't bother us that we didn't have a lot of in depth conversations with others. Just enjoy the diversity! And relax! That's what you're there for, right????

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent All-Inclusive and affordable We have just returned from a weeks stay at Carabela Beach Resort and couldn't wait to write our review after seeing so many poor reviews prior to leaving on our trip, they actually had us pretty concerned that we had made a bad choice. Not so at all! We plan to return next year for the following reasons. First of all I have read so many complaints about the food! Well we thought the numerous choices were aplenty and always found more than enough that we thought was great and by the looks of other peoples plate mounded high I don't think they had many complaints either! I never heard of any one getting sick, and the bottled water is offered everywhere you turned! We tried all 3 restaurants and they were very nice also, a change from the buffet, but we were always glad to have the buffet again the next night. The beach grill was okay except we did not care for the hamburgs so most days we went back to the buffet for lunch, often making grilled cheese sandwiches on freshly baked bread, had some sort of pasta salad as a side and the desserts were always varied and very good. We especially liked the flan, ice cream and variety of fresh fruits at every meal. Our room was fine, it was in the 5000 building, an older building but the ocean view was wonderful, beautiful sunrises, and well tended to by the maid service daily, (suggest leaving a daily tip and we brought small inexpensive treats for her too. In return she left us flowers and plenty of TP! Yes, bring your own face cloths if you use them! A good time to get rid of the tattered ones we all have in our closets. The grounds were absolutely gorgeous and the grounds keepers were busily maintaining them every day, we saw the pools being cleaned daily also. The beach did have lots of shady areas, but many people like that and we always had our same sunny area everyday without having to get up and out early to reserve a chair. The weather, beach and ocean were lovely. We arose early and were in our rooms by 10pm so did not partake in the disco or casino. We just wanted RR and got just that! Of course there were plenty of beach and water activities and aerobics going on but we preferred to relax, read, swim and even had massages on the beach, $25 for a half hour. El Corcheito, the little town right next door was a convenient place to walk to. Of course you have the usual merchants all wanting you to see their shops, like many other places I have visited. They will take lower prices because they want your business. We found a few gifts for friends and ourselves without spending much $. We met a few other English speaking guests to talk to but it was not an issue with us because our jobs require lots an lots of talking so it was a nice change to just chill! In closing we had a very enjoyable vacation and recommend Carbela as a great place to vacation, there were all age groups there and not one person appeared to be having a bad time.

<Content>very happy with this resort!!!!! my family stayed at this resort from 2/24-3/3 2006 there were 11 of us ages 4-63 yrs. old. i have to say after reading some of the reviews before we left i was alittle nervous....the transition from the airport to the hotel was alittle long...we were the last ones to be dropped off we had made 3 other stops to drop at other resorts so a 14 mile ride turned into and hour and a half!!!oh well no biggie...check in was great andre at the front desk put our 3 rooms in building 2 together that made things convient we had rooms overlooking the main pool and dinner area it was beautiful!!!!we were on the 3rd floor and the elevator did work although we opted to do the stairs always...good exercise...the room itself was very clean but did have a musty damp smell but its the caribbean its hot and humid all the time!!!!the a/c worked great and sometimes we did without it and kept the slider open..our maid was superb her name is luz maria my son got the flu while we were there (vomiting and diarrhea) and she would check in on him often and completely scoured the room with bleach...no one else got sick thank god!!!the pool and beach were very clean and very easy to get to short walks to anywhere in the resort made it very nice!!the food was alittle different i think its geared more toward the european palate..we are american and i guess had a fabulous time i would recommend this resort to anyone!!!i think a vacation is all what you make of it get involved learn other cultures if was a great learning experience i too can't wait to go back!!!!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Dissapointed Rooms: Unless you get some of the newer rooms, be prepared for rock hard beds and pillows that were uncomfortable and mould ridden. The air conditioning was mediocre and the water pressure was terrible and there was no hot water the first night after a long flight and late arrival. Maid service was good and room was cleaned consistently each afternoon. Better to leave a bit of a tip each day, since there may be different staff on throughout your stay. The room had a lightbulb missing along with a musty smell in the room and as I mentioned low pressure and no hot water the first night - when it was mentioned to the travel rep, she relayed it quickly and in all instances the maintenance staff were quick to respond. Food: There was mounds of food beautifully displayed, BUT... it was tasteless and there was little change in the menu at the main al a carte each day. Things would show up the next meal or day disguised as some stange salad - one even had chopped up weiners in it YUCK! Desserts looked spectacular but were terribly bland. The fresh baked bread was nice and so were the dinner rolls. The other restaraunts were terrible. It was basically the same type of food with personal service. The burito was deep fried??? and the crepe was a piece of flat dough with caramel sauce and a scoop of ice cream. I passed on that.There is not much to each outside of the al a carte. The food hut on the beach served burgers, fries, hotdogs and pizza - ALL TERRIBLE. The only good thing there was the soft serve ice cream.Beach: Very nice, but quite shady. Mix of a type of tropical pine with palms. There were mini-cones on the beach that hurt when you stepped on them. Water was fairly calm and 98% sunshine. The beaches are very similar to ones I have been to in Florida - more natural than manicured. This is personal preference I suppose.Hotel: Be prepared to watch your step in the evening. They apprear to ration their lights (electricity) and paths are not well lit at night. Even hotel stairwells, seem to have alternate floors lit. I think this was deliberate to conserve energy. The only afternoon it was overcast, the staff had to be asked to turn the lights on in the restaurant. Overall the hotel entry was well polished, but again with little lighting it had a dingy appearance.Pools: Seemed find to me clean and well maintained.Drinks: I sampled a few and then stuck to water and the beer. Poor drink presentation and poorly made. The coffee was dispensed only at breakfast and dinner by a machine - it tasted instant and was horrible.English Speaking: There were mostly Europeans at this location and very few Canadians or Americans to chat with. I didn't find any overt rudeness as some other reviews stated, but it made it difficult to chat with others while there.Overall, the grounds were beautiful, the beach fine and the service ok. I would not go back there and think I might try Cuba next year! I have family going to Peurto Plata in spring, so will be interested in comparing their notes against my stay in Punta Cana.  
<Date>Feb 24, 2006

<Content>Not Bad My wife and I spent the week of Jan 27 to Feb 3 at Club Carabela. We stayed in the 10,000 block which are the newest units. Still there was a few poblems such as the air conditioner wasn't working and the room smelled musty. We moved to another room and than everything was okay. The food at the buffet wasn't bad; however, it was never hot. The coffee was bad which is surprizing for the DR. Of course the drinks were good and the bar service was great. The weather was fantastic and the pools (3) were clean. The beach was nice but there were too many trees and not enough sun. We met some real nice people and maybe lasting friends.This resort was reasonable for the money that we paid ($749 Cdn).Chris and Donna

<Author>carlsojo
<Content>sorry folks this place stinks First off some backround. Me and my girlfriend visited this resort between march 15th to the 22nd 2005 We are in our early thirties and are middle class from minnesota. Im late on this review because I was just dis interested in taking the time to write this after a vacation. Were going to mexico this year and wish I would have heeded the warnings from the not so great reviews on carabela. Rooms: Check in went fine the people are very sincere and helpful. Our first room had a huge crack across the patio door, not a good first impression. We got our second room quick enough, I tried to open the patio door and the handle fell off. The drain in the tub was clogged, the lights didnt work, the ac was a joke. The tv was tiny I mean tiny. The gaps in the door were so big a 6 year old could have jimmied it open with a butter knife. If you insist on going to this resort make sure you get a room in the newer buildings, much nicer.Food: People trust me when I say the food was just horrible. Im not a picky person but its the same warmed up crap every single day!!! The so called resturaunts arent much better, it was like the buffet food served to you with a fancy plate and a waiter. The beach grill is not what one might invision folks. Its not like theres some guy out there on a open pit hot grill serving up great burgers and all beef weinies, its a joke cold steamed hot dogs, hamburgers pre cooked stacked a mile high in the open hot air. Sounds yummy eh. I did get a burger and then I barely made it back to my room to you know what. We did not get sick from the food. Just stay away from those beach burgers!!!!The beach: The beach was great, no complaints. swimming in the ocean was great the weather was just awesome. What bothered me is that you had to leave a deposit to use any swim gear like snorkles and such. what a hassle, I usually dont carry cash when I wanna go in the ocean.The resort: The grounds on the resort are kept up very nice, the pools are nice except for the filthy one in the front with the swim up bar. The drinks are not top shelf, That was no biggie to me, Hey they were all free. The peacocks on the resort are annoying. At first you think hey thats cool look at those pretty birds, by the second night you find yourself wishing you had a shotgun. They quackle and whine while your eating, they are in the buffet building pecking at scraps and stairing at you, trust me on this one the birds gotta go.The people: The Dominican people are the nicest people on earth. The wait staff the bartenders were just awesome. I know this review is not flattering to the resort but I really dont want to take away the fact that the local people are just wonderful!!!! As for our friends the europeans???? Well what would you expect from such a cultured society. We meet some great people from the states.Overall: We actually had a pretty good time looking back on it. I know some of this might sound nit picky or something like that but I wish I would have listened to the negative reviews. To me when the food is horrible and the room is just as bad its hard to enjoy yourself for 7 nights, remember 7 nights. At the end we basically were eating bread with butter and oreos from the little convienance store. Were fun people and like to tipp a few so we made the best of it.In closing: Hey spend a little more on yourself and go to were the reviews are constant 5s and 4s with a 3 thrown in from time to time. This year were going to mexico all inclusive 5 star for sure, yea its gonna cost about $250 more per person but every review for this place is 5 or 4. Well good luck and if your all set to go to carabela have a good time and just know I tried to help.
